<Review>Great for inexpensive produce that always looks nice and fresh, plus a few other things. Dry goods like rice, beans pasta and lentils. Milk, eggs, some deli meat. Imported sweets. Olive oils. Jam. Jars of veggies. Dolmas. Sardines and other canned fish. Honey. Some breads and pita.

Cheese selection is mostly ethnic and most cheese you might expect to find in a typical American grocery won't be found here. It's been cool to try some of these that I have never seen before.

<text>This is the second location to open (the first in the city of Napa). A third location is on the way!

Fantastic cal-latin breakfast and lunch oriented foods with a little something for everyone.

Feeling hung over from tasting all day and stumbling into Panchas the day before, then throw down on some Biscuits and Gravy or a Croque Senora. Both are warm heavy and filling options. Eating light and fresh? Rock out with a quinoa breakfast bowl or farro salad. Don't worry, if you're feeling basic they have a great avocado toast.

Mostly outside seating but they do have blankets. Combo that blanket with some wine and you'll be fine.

< Review>
Your basic self-serve car wash. Vacuums with decent suction before the wash ($1 for 4 minutes). The wash itself is standard, one brush and one water gun. I feel like the prices for this place are actually pretty reasonable ($3 for 5 minutes and +), especially given it's convenient location. You can use cash or their own tokens. You can pretty comfortably wash/vacuum your car for $10.</Review>

<Rate>4< /Rate>< Review>
Pretty good self service car wash. The stalls are a bit smaller than other places so if you have a large vehicle you might want to check it out before you deposit $$. Other than that it has most of the things that you could want at a self service car wash. Accepts cash or card. One thing I might suggest that other places have are hand blow dryers to dry the car off. These are a very nice feature. There is a good amount of space after pulling out of the stall to hand dry your vehicle.< /Review>

< review>
Overall really great for people in PB without covered parking or water access at their homes.

Pros
Good prices at $3 for 5 min then up from there.  When my smaller car is just slightly dirty I go with touch less and I just do low pressure presoak>high pressure soap>spot free rinse, and can finish in 5-7 minutes so less than $5 for a quick wash.

For washes where I actually wipe down the car I finish in 10-12 min easily which doesn‚Äôt cost much more

Takes credit cards!  (Tho occasionally they don‚Äôt work)
Spot free rinse makes life easy

Cons

No hand washing - for someone with a new car like me I am NOT using their foaming brush for free scratches on my car, period.  If no one is around though I do bring my own mitt and as long as you aren‚Äôt washing without the timer running, and no one is waiting behind you, I don‚Äôt think anyone is going to kick you out.  I usually will carry the foaming brush and use the foam dropping out to coat the car and scrub while I go around the car.

Vacuums are meh - Probably just depends on your luck tho if u go after some dummy clogs up the tube before you.

< Text>
What a beautiful, scenic venue to taste excellent wines. The staff is very friendly and eager to share a plethora of info about grapes, winemaking and wine in general and Matchbook Wines in particular. There was no charge for the tasting. Bottles are very reasonably priced. The only thing lacking is the opportunity to purchase cheese and crackers or other snacks (if you don't come when a food truck event is occurring). So, bring your own munchies if you want to drink up.<//Text>

<Text>What should have been a wonderful winetasting experience was a great disappointment for me and my friend when we visited Matchbook as soon as it opened its doors one weekend morning.  I was excited about visiting this winery because I was particularly interested in tasting its Sauvignon blanc.  After paying what I thought was a rather steep tasting fee given the area and limited number of wine tastes offered, I became further disillusioned when the pourer informed me in no uncertain terms that they were not serving the Sauvignon blanc that day even though it was on the list.  Once she stepped away from the serving area and a senior staff member came by, I had the opportunity to gently express to him how disappointed I was to learn that they were not pouring my favorite wine that day. He took the young lady aside, chatted with her a bit, and the next thing I knew we were tasting the Sauvignon blanc!  While he saved the day for us, due to our pourer's attitude we won't be returning to Matchbook anytime soon.< /Text><Resp>None</Resp>< username>

< Text>
Hands down, a wonderful dining experience. The atmosphere very relaxing and beautiful in their new out door seating area. The service was stellar, as expected. We ordered a sampler plate for appetizer. Everything was great and the portions were perfect. Our table ordered salmon, filet mignon and lobster. Everything was cooked to perfection. <userid>114480842719328908445< /userid>< name>
Brett C< /name>
<time>1618932880229< /time>< Rate>
5</Rate>
< text>
My wife and I needed a breakfast spot while in the area, and man am I glad I decided to eat at Spencer's!

We started with some mimosas and coffee. Coffee was excellent, and the mimosas were tasty--you can always tell when a place uses fresh OJ to make the mimosas.

We were starving, so we really pigged out! I had the breakfast sandwich on a buttery croissant, and OMG it was amazing. A perfectly cooked couple of eggs, ham, and bacon, all stuffed with ooey, gooey cheddar cheese. I'm a bit of a breakfast sandwich connoisseur--I've eaten many, from many different places, so I know a good one when I have one, and this is at worst the 2nd best one I've ever had, possibly the best ever. Served with hash browns which were also perfectly cooked, and not soggy at all like so many places make them. My wife had the traditional eggs benedict, and she loved it as well. The hollandaise was on point. We also shared the Spencer's waffle as a dessert at the end, and it was OK, I just wish they put the fruit on the side, as I felt the waffle lost its crispiness due to the fruit being placed on top. In fairness my wife said the fruit on top didn't affect the waffle from her point of view.

Service was EXCELLENT as well. Professional, prompt, and on top of everything.

All in all, I very, very highly recommend you get breakfast at Spencer's if you're in the area. You can thank me later :)<//text>

< Review>
Found this place online and it does not disappoint. Stunning backyard with giant trees & romantic lighting. Food was excellent. We got the prix-fixe menu for $38. Came with soup du jour (mushroom truffle oil soup), entree (sesame crusted salmon with coconut rice and garlic asparagus), and dessert (pot de creme & cookies). Ordered the $2 drink on the menu and actually really liked it. Refreshing, not too heavy. Perfect on a hot day! They serve bread on the house that was clearly home made and delicious. Highly recommend reservations. We had reservations at 7:30pm and were seated immediately, but I noted the restaurant (indoor & patio) was packed. Recommend sitting outdoors on patio. They have misters in summer and in wintertime over 30 heaters. You can valet for $3 or self-park for free on the roadside.< /Review>

<date>1541479715568< /date><Rate>5<//Rate><text>Upscale dining in Palm Springs, with all the expected class and quality of food preparation.  A 3 course fix prix menu offers true value for the Palm Springs area.

I f you do get to visit, watching the well trained staff is a genuine pleasurable entertainment today.  The wait staff is trained in timing as well as proper service techniques.  One never feels rushed, like one does in most eating establishments in  the US.  It seems almost French or Italian in leisurely pacing.

This brings me to an interesting point here as in most US restaurants.  One can buy a couple of glasses of house wine for around $10 a glass at least if not more for something of quality.  Why not buy a bottle of wine for $40-50 for the same amount of higher quality wine?  Of course, pricier bottles are less of a value, but Spencer's offers reasonably priced bottles, so why purchase inferior glasses of wine?  I wish some restaurants would be creative enough to offer a genuinely creative tasting wine offering every evening with unique and attractive and daily changing wine selections.</text>< Pics>

<user>110204891685770336136</user><username>Ted Inoue</username><Date>1421970049180< /Date><Rate>4</Rate>< text>
I find it difficult to rate Spencer's. It's very chic and the service was exceptional and the prix fixe menu was a pretty good value. The setting was also quite pretty they were clear knock off of another place in town. The disappointment really came to the food which was mediocre at best. I mean it wasn't bad and I enjoyed my short rib, but a place like this deserves a much better more inspired menu and preparation. If this place were back home, I wouldn't be returning. But here I had an enjoyable enough night that I'd give them 4-stars.
To summarize, if you're a real foodie, I'd skip this place and go to one of the more interesting restaurants in town. But if you're on a date and don't want to break the bank it's hard to beat it.<//text>

< Text>
This is my favorite restaurant in this valley.  The food that I have had here over the years has been fresh, beautifully prepared, and delicious, but I have to admit that even if it were not, I would still be enchanted by this place.  I always ask for a table on the patio, whether it is lunch or dinner, and I'm never disappointed by the experience - the ambience is simply beautiful.  The patio/terrace is enclosed by walls of windows, which do much to cut the wind and cool air during the winter months, along with judicious use of heat lamps.  Sparkling ornamental lights dangle from the trees, and are reflected in the many panes of glass surrounding the terrace, to produce a magical atmosphere.  We find ourselves sighing and remarking how blissful it is to eat outside under such conditions several times during any meal!

As for the food, I have enjoyed everything I have eaten here.  My favorites include the beef shortribs (meat falling off the bone tender) and the whitefish.  And the prix fixe menu makes it pretty affordable in spite of the fact that it is one of the valley's premier restaurants.<//Text>

My wife and I were in Palm Springs on business. We were looking for a restaurant that was affordable, yet offered quality food, great service and a great atmosphere. I've been to many nice restaurants in my life from all different price ranges and rarely do you find such a perfect combination of all 3 at any price range, yet alone at such a value as this place. < text>
I surprised my boyfriend for his 50th birthday for dinner here, which was both our first time at this restaurant. I brought a special decorated cake ahead of time to be served after dinner as a surprise that they kept for our reservation which we showed up early for. We were greeted friendly and taken straight to our patio table which I had requested ahead of time. Although a bit pricey, everything we ordered was amazing!!! We both had the filet mignon and the service was very professional. The ambience was perfectly romantic and they brought out the cake right on time and even greeted my boyfriend with a happy birthday wish as we placed our order telling me that he was aware of the surprise cake situation. Everything went as expected and we both were impressed and excited to return. Thank you Spencer's =)<//text>

On April 17, 2016 Palm Springs California I called the restaurant spencers to let them know prior that I was coming in with one other person to have a complementary lunch brunch.  During this brief time in the foyer area of the restaurant the hostess was rude said there was nothing she could do because it was no manager on site at the time.

My review of spencers restaurant in Palm Springs California will stand.

1. Cold food

3.  Non-alcoholic drinks  served with alcohol
